0)
{








apply_ad_config(google_ads.length);









render_ads(true,
window['ad_config_top']);









if(window['backfillParam'])
{












window['backfillParam']['pl_rnum']
=
google_ads.length;












window['backfillParam']['pl_time']
=
Date.now()
-
afc_ad_start_time;








}




}
}

function
apply_ad_config(num)
{
window['ad_config_top']
=
Math.min(2,
num);
window['ad_config_bot']
=
Math.min(2,
num);
}

google_ad_client
=
'ca-aj-cat';
google_ad_channel
=
'cx_ask_wiki,ad_dirN';
google_ad_output
=
'js';
google_max_num_ads
=
'4';
google_ad_type
=
'text';
google_image_size
=
'';
google_num_ads_recieved=
'';
google_language
=
'';
google_country
=
'';
google_encoding
=
'utf8';
google_safe
=
'medium';
google_adtest
=
'off';
google_ad_section
=
'default';
google_page_url
=
'';
google_hints
=
'Bon_Jovi';
google_kw
=
'';
google_kw_type
=
'broad';


var
backfillParam
=
{




pl_rqnum
:
google_max_num_ads,




pl_hints
:
google_hints,




pl_rp
:
"false",




pl_kw
:
google_kw,




pl_cl
:
google_ad_client,




pl_ch
:
google_ad_channel,




pl_hex
:
"#FDFEEE",




pl_type
:
"afc",




pl_clksp
:
"none"};

var
word_arr
;

var
word_arr_len
;


function
highlightQuery(input_str)
{

var
queryTokenArray
=
"bon,jovi,_,";


var
tok_arr
=
queryTokenArray.split(",");

for(tok_arr_idx=0;
tok_arr_idx
<
tok_arr.length-1;
tok_arr_idx
++)
{

if(isCombinationWord(tok_arr[tok_arr_idx])){
word_arr
=
tok_arr[tok_arr_idx].split("-");
word_arr_len
=
word_arr.length;
first_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(word_arr[0],0);

if(first_pos
!=-1)
{
input_str
=
highlightCombinationWords(input_str,first_pos);
}
}
else
{
first_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(tok_arr[tok_arr_idx],0);
if(first_pos
!=
-1
&&
tok_arr[tok_arr_idx].length
>
0)
{
input_str
=
highlightSimpleWords(input_str,tok_arr[tok_arr_idx],first_pos);
}
}
}
return
input_str;
}

function
isCombinationWord(word){
if(word.indexOf("-")
!=
-1){
return
true;
}
else
{
return
false;
}
}


function
isAlpha(ch)
{
if
(ch
!=
null
&&
ch.match(/^[a-zA-Z0-9]+$/)){
return
true;
}
return
false;
}

function
isQueryinInput(firstindex,
input_str,
j){
for(i=firstindex;
i<
input_str.length
;
++i)
{
var
currindex
=
i;

if(!isAlpha(input_str.charAt(i)))
{
if(firstindex
==
currindex)

{
firstindex++;
}
else
{
if(word_arr[j]
!=
input_str.substring(firstindex,currindex).toLowerCase())
return
-1;
if
(j
==
word_arr_len-1)
return
currindex;
else
return
isQueryinInput(currindex+1,input_str,++j);
}
}
}

if(j
<
word_arr_len)
{
if(word_arr[j]
!=
input_str.substring(firstindex,currindex+1).toLowerCase())
return
-1;
}

return
(currindex
+
1)
;
}


function

highlightCombinationWords(input_str,first_pos)
{
exactmatch
=
isQueryinInput(first_pos+word_arr[0].length,input_str,1)
;
if(exactmatch
!=-1
)

{
bold_str
=
"<b>"
+
input_str.substring(first_pos,exactmatch)
+
"</b>";
input_str
=
input_str.substring(0,first_pos)
+
bold_str
+
input_str.substring(exactmatch);
next_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(word_arr[0],exactmatch+7);
while(next_pos
!=
-1)
{
return
highlightCombinationWords(input_str,next_pos);
}
}
return
input_str;
}


function

highlightSimpleWords(input_str,token,
first_pos)
{
var
end_pos
=
first_pos
+
token.length;
if(!isAlpha(input_str.charAt(end_pos))
&&
!isAlpha(input_str.charAt(first_pos-1))){
bold_str
=
"<b>"
+
input_str.substring(first_pos,end_pos)
+
"</b>";
input_str
=
input_str.substring(0,first_pos)
+
bold_str
+
input_str.substring(end_pos);
next_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(token,end_pos+7);
}
else
{
next_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(token,end_pos);
}

while(next_pos
!=
-1)
{
return
highlightSimpleWords(input_str,token,next_pos);
}
return
input_str;
}</script>

<p><b>Bon
Jovi</b>
is
an
<a
href="/wiki/United_States_of_America?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="United
States
of
America"
class="mw-redirect">American</a>
<a
href="/wiki/Rock_music?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rock
music">rock</a>
band
from
<a
href="/wiki/Sayreville,_New_Jersey?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Sayreville,
New
Jersey">Sayreville,
New
Jersey</a>.
Formed
in
1983,
Bon
Jovi
consists
of
lead
singer
and
namesake
<a
href="/wiki/Jon_Bon_Jovi?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Jon
Bon
Jovi">Jon
Bon
Jovi</a>
(John
Francis
Bongiovi,
Jr.),
guitarist
<a
href="/wiki/Richie_Sambora?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Richie
Sambora">Richie
Sambora</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/David_Bryan?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="David
Bryan">David
Bryan</a>,
and
drummer
<a
href="/wiki/Tico_Torres?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Tico
Torres">Tico
Torres</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-historyking_1-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-historyking-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
band's
lineup
has
remained
mostly
static
during
its
history,
the
only
exception
being
the
1994
dismissal
of
bass
player
<a
href="/wiki/Alec_John_Such?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Alec
John
Such">Alec
John
Such</a>,
who
was
unofficially
replaced
by
<a
href="/wiki/Hugh_McDonald_(American_musician)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hugh
McDonald
(American
musician)">Hugh
McDonald</a>.
In
1986,
Bon
Jovi
achieved
widespread
global
recognition
with
their
third
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Slippery_When_Wet?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Slippery
When
Wet">Slippery
When
Wet</a></i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
band's
fourth
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/New_Jersey_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="New
Jersey
(album)">New
Jersey</a></i>
was
equally
successful
in
1988.
After
touring
and
recording
non-stop
during
the
late
1980s,
the
band
went
on
hiatus
following
the
<a
href="/wiki/New_Jersey_Tour?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="New
Jersey
Tour"
class="mw-redirect">New
Jersey
Tour</a>
in
1990,
during
which
time
Jon
Bon
Jovi
and
Richie
Sambora
both
released
successful
solo
albums.
In
1992,
the
band
returned
with
the
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/Keep_the_Faith?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Keep
the
Faith">Keep
the
Faith</a></i>.
Their
2000
single
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/It%27s_My_Life_(Bon_Jovi_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="It's
My
Life
(Bon
Jovi
song)">It's
My
Life</a>&quot;,
which
followed
a
second
hiatus,
successfully
introduced
the
band
to
a
younger
audience.
Bon
Jovi
have
been
known
to
use
different
styles
in
their
music,
which
has
included
<a
href="/wiki/Country_music?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Country
music">country</a>
for
their
2007
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/Lost_Highway_(Bon_Jovi_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Lost
Highway
(Bon
Jovi
album)">Lost
Highway</a></i>.
On
March
12,
2013,
Bon
Jovi
released
their
12th
studio
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/What_About_Now_(Bon_Jovi_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="What
About
Now
(Bon
Jovi
album)"
class="mw-redirect">What
About
Now</a></i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-BecauseWeCan_3-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-BecauseWeCan-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Thus
far,
Bon
Jovi
has
released
12
<a
href="/wiki/Studio_album?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Studio
album"
class="mw-redirect">studio
albums</a>,
plus
three
<a
href="/wiki/Compilation_album?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Compilation
album">compilations</a>
and
two
<a
href="/wiki/Live_albums?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Live
albums"
class="mw-redirect">live
albums</a>.
They
are
one
of
the
<a
href="/wiki/List_of_best-selling_music_artists?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="List
of
best-selling
music
artists">world’s
best-selling
bands
of
all
time</a>,
having
sold
more
than
130
million
records
worldwide,<sup
id="cite_ref-dp-bonjovi_4-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-dp-bonjovi-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
performed
more
than
2,700
concerts
in
over
50
countries
for
more
than
34
million
fans.<sup
id="cite_ref-Bon_top40-charts.com_5-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Bon_top40-charts.com-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup>
Bon
Jovi
was
inducted
into
the
<a
href="/wiki/UK_Music_Hall_of_Fame?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="UK
Music
Hall
of
Fame">UK
Music
Hall
of
Fame</a>
in
2006.<sup
id="cite_ref-Bon_Jovi_to_enter_UK_Hall_of_Fame_6-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Bon_Jovi_to_enter_UK_Hall_of_Fame-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
band
was
also
honored
with
the
Award
of
Merit
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/American_Music_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="American
Music
Awards"
class="mw-redirect">American
Music
Awards</a>
in
2004,<sup
id="cite_ref-Bon_Jovi_honored_at_American_Music_Awards_7-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Bon_Jovi_honored_at_American_Music_Awards-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
as
songwriters
and
collaborators,
Jon
Bon
Jovi
and
Richie
Sambora
were
inducted
into
<a
href="/wiki/Songwriters_Hall_of_Fame?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Songwriters
Hall
of
Fame">Songwriters
Hall
of
Fame</a>
in
2009.<sup
id="cite_ref-Jon_SongHall_8-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Jon_SongHall-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-Richie_SongHall_9-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Richie_SongHall-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<p><a
href="/wiki/Jon_Bon_Jovi?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Jon
Bon
Jovi">Jon
Bon
Jovi</a>
began
playing
piano
and
guitar
in
1975,
at
the
age
of
13,
with
his
first
band
'Raze'.
At
16,
Bon
Jovi
met
<a
href="/wiki/David_Bryan?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="David
Bryan">David
Bryan</a>
and
formed
a
band
called
&quot;Atlantic
City
Expressway&quot;.
Still
in
his
teens,
Bon
Jovi
played
in
the
band
&quot;John
Bongiovi
and
the
Wild
Ones,&quot;
playing
local
clubs
like
&quot;The
Fast
Lane,&quot;
and
opening
for
known
acts
in
the
area.
By
1980,
he
formed
another
band,
&quot;The
Rest&quot;,
and
opened
up
for
New
Jersey
acts
such
as
<a
href="/wiki/Southside_Johnny_and_the_Asbury_Jukes?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Southside
Johnny
and
the
Asbury
Jukes"
class="mw-redirect">Southside
Johnny
and
the
Asbury
Jukes</a>.</p>








<p>By
mid-1982,
out
of
school
and
working
part-time
at
a
women's
shoe
store,
Jon
Bon
Jovi
took
a
job
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/Avatar_Studios?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Avatar
Studios">Power
Station
Studios</a>,
a
<a
href="/wiki/Manhattan?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Manhattan">Manhattan</a>
recording
facility
where
his
cousin
Tony
Bongiovi
was
co-owner.
Bon
Jovi
made
several
<a
href="/wiki/Demo_(music)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Demo
(music)">demos</a>—including
one
produced
by
<a
href="/wiki/Billy_Squier?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Billy
Squier">Billy
Squier</a>—and
sent
them
to
record
companies,
though
failing
to
make
an
impact.
His
first
professional
recording
was
as
lead
vocals
in
&quot;R2-D2
We
Wish
You
a
Merry
Christmas,&quot;
which
was
part
of
the
<i><a
href="/wiki/Christmas_in_the_Stars?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Christmas
in
the
Stars">Christmas
in
the
Stars</a></i>
album
which
his
cousin
co-produced.</p>








<p>Bon
Jovi
visited
local
radio
station
<a
href="/wiki/WAPP_103.5FM_%22The_Apple%22?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="WAPP
103.5FM
&quot;The
Apple&quot;"
class="mw-redirect">WAPP
103.5FM
&quot;The
Apple&quot;</a>
in
<a
href="/wiki/Lake_Success,_New_York?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Lake
Success,
New
York">Lake
Success</a>,
New
York.
In
1983,
a
then-unknown
Bon
Jovi
visited
the
station
and
wrote
and
sung
the
jingles
for
the
station.
He
spoke
with
DJ
Chip
Hobart
and
to
the
promotion
director,
John
Lassman,
who
suggested
Bon
Jovi
let
WAPP
include
the
song
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Runaway_(Bon_Jovi_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Runaway
(Bon
Jovi
song)">Runaway</a>&quot;
on
the
station's
compilation
album
of
local
homegrown
talent.
Bon
Jovi
was
reluctant,
but
eventually
gave
them
the
song,
on
which
Bon
Jovi
had
used
studio
musicians
to
play
on
the
track
&quot;Runaway&quot;
(which
was
written
in
1982).
WAPP
worked
with
WOR-TV
(now
WWOR-TV)
in
nearby
Secaucus,
NJ
on
a
music
video
show,
Rock
9
Videos,
for
a
short
time
in
1984.
The
studio
musicians
who
helped
record
&quot;Runaway&quot;—known
as
The
All
Star
Review—were
guitarist
Tim
Pierce,
keyboardist
<a
href="/wiki/Roy_Bittan?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Roy
Bittan">Roy
Bittan</a>,
drummer
<a
href="/wiki/Frankie_LaRocka?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Frankie
LaRocka">Frankie
LaRocka</a>,
and
bassist
<a
href="/wiki/Hugh_McDonald_(American_musician)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hugh
McDonald
(American
musician)">Hugh
McDonald</a>.</p>








<div
class="thumb
tright">









<div
class="thumbinner"
style="width:222px;">









<a
href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Bon_Jovi_O2_Arena_Circle_Tour.JPG"
target="_blank"
class="image"><img
alt=""
src="http://rpmedia.ask.com/ts?u=/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Bon_Jovi_O2_Arena_Circle_Tour.JPG/220px-Bon_Jovi_O2_Arena_Circle_Tour.JPG"
width="220"
height="165"
class="thumbimage"
srcset="http://rpmedia.ask.com/ts?u=/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Bon_Jovi_O2_Arena_Circle_Tour.JPG/330px-Bon_Jovi_O2_Arena_Circle_Tour.JPG
1.5x,
http://rpmedia.ask.com/ts?u=/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Bon_Jovi_O2_Arena_Circle_Tour.JPG/440px-Bon_Jovi_O2_Arena_Circle_Tour.JPG
2x"
/></a>










<div
class="thumbcaption">











<div
class="magnify">











<a
href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Bon_Jovi_O2_Arena_Circle_Tour.JPG"
target="_blank"
class="internal"
title="Enlarge"><img
src="http://sp.ask.com/sh/i/wiki/magnify-clip.png"
width="15"
height="11"
alt=""
/></a>










</div>
Jon
Bon
Jovi
and
Richie
Sambora
on
stage









</div>









</div>








</div>








<p>The
song
began
to
get
airplay
in
the
New
York
area,
then
other
sister
stations
in
major
markets
picked
up
the
song.
In
March
1983,
Bon
Jovi
called
David
Bryan,
who
in
turn
called
bassist
<a
href="/wiki/Alec_John_Such?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Alec
John
Such">Alec
John
Such</a>
and
an
experienced
drummer
named
<a
href="/wiki/Tico_Torres?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Tico
Torres">Tico
Torres</a>,
both
formerly
of
the
band
Phantom's
Opera.
Tapped
to
play
lead
guitar
was
Bon
Jovi's
neighbor,
<a
href="/wiki/Dave_Sabo?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Dave
Sabo">Dave
Sabo</a>
(a.k.a.
The
Snake)—although
he
never
officially
joined
the
band.
He
and
Jon
promised
each
other
that
whoever
made
it
first,
would
help
out
the
other.
He
later
went
on
to
form
the
group
<a
href="/wiki/Skid_Row_(American_band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Skid
Row
(American
band)">Skid
Row</a>.
Jon
saw
and
was
impressed
with
hometown
guitarist
Richie
Sambora.
Sambora
had
toured
with
<a
href="/wiki/Joe_Cocker?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Joe
Cocker">Joe
Cocker</a>,
played
with
a
group
called
<a
href="/wiki/Mercy_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Mercy
(band)">Mercy</a>
and
had
been
called
up
to
audition
for
<a
href="/wiki/Kiss_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Kiss
(band)">Kiss</a>.
He
also
played
on
the
album
<i>Lessons</i>
with
the
band
Message,
which
was
re-released
on
<a
href="/wiki/CD?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="CD"
class="mw-redirect">CD</a>
through
Long
Island
Records
in
1995.
Message
was
originally
signed
to
<a
href="/wiki/Led_Zeppelin?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Led
Zeppelin">Led
Zeppelin</a>'s
<a
href="/wiki/Swan_Song_Records?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Swan
Song
Records">Swan
Song
Records</a>
label,
although
the
album
was
never
released.</p>








<p>Tico
Torres
was
also
an
experienced
musician,
having
recorded
and
played
live
with
Phantom's
Opera,
<a
href="/wiki/The_Marvelettes?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Marvelettes">The
Marvelettes</a>,
and
<a
href="/wiki/Chuck_Berry?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Chuck
Berry">Chuck
Berry</a>.
He
appeared
on
26
records
and
had
recently
recorded
with
<a
href="/wiki/Franke_and_the_Knockouts?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Franke
and
the
Knockouts">Franke
and
the
Knockouts</a>,
a
Jersey
band
with
hit
singles
during
the
early
1980s.</p>








<p>David
Bryan
had
quit
the
band
that
he
and
Bon
Jovi
had
founded
in
order
to
study
medicine.
While
in
college,
he
realized
that
he
wanted
to
pursue
music
full-time,
and
was
accepted
to
<a
href="/wiki/Juilliard_School?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Juilliard
School">Juilliard
School</a>,
a
New
York
music
school.
When
Bon
Jovi
called
his
friend
and
said
that
he
was
putting
together
a
band,
and
a
record
deal
looked
likely,
Bryan
followed
Bon
Jovi's
lead
and
gave
up
his
studies.</p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Bon_Jovi_and_7800.C2.B0_Fahrenheit_.281984.E2.80.931985.29"><i>Bon
Jovi</i>
and
<i>7800&deg;
Fahrenheit</i>
(1984–1985)</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Bon_Jovi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3"
title="Edit
section:
Bon
Jovi
and
7800&deg;
Fahrenheit
(1984–1985)">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>Once
the
band
began
playing
showcases
and
opening
for
local
talent,
they
caught
the
attention
of
record
executive
<a
href="/wiki/Derek_Shulman?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Derek
Shulman">Derek
Shulman</a>,
who
signed
them
to
<a
href="/wiki/Mercury_Records?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Mercury
Records">Mercury
Records</a>
and
who
was
part
of
the
<a
href="/wiki/PolyGram?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="PolyGram">PolyGram</a>
company.
Because
Jon
Bon
Jovi
wanted
a
group
name,
Pamela
Maher,
a
friend
of
Richard
Fischer
and
an
employee
of
<a
href="/wiki/Doc_McGhee?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Doc
McGhee">Doc
McGhee</a>,
suggested
they
call
themselves
Bon
Jovi,
following
the
example
of
the
other
famous
two-word
bands
such
as
<a
href="/wiki/Van_Halen?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Van
Halen">Van
Halen</a>.
This
name
was
chosen
instead
of
the
original
idea
of
Johnny
Electric.
Pamela's
suggestion
of
the
name
was
met
with
little
enthusiasm,
but
two
years
later
they
hit
the
charts
under
that
name.</p>








<p>With
the
help
of
their
new
manager
<a
href="/wiki/Doc_McGhee?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Doc
McGhee">Doc
McGhee</a>
they
recorded
the
band's
debut
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Bon_Jovi_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bon
Jovi
(album)">Bon
Jovi</a></i>,
which
was
released
on
January
21,
1984.
The
album
included
the
band's
first
hit
single,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Runaway_(Bon_Jovi_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Runaway
(Bon
Jovi
song)">Runaway</a>&quot;,
reaching
top
forty
on
the
<a
href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Billboard
Hot
100">Billboard
Hot
100</a>.
The
album
peaked
at
number
forty-three
on
the
<a
href="/wiki/Billboard_200?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Billboard
200">Billboard
200</a>
album
chart.
The
group
soon
found
itself
opening
for
<a
href="/wiki/Scorpions_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Scorpions
(band)">Scorpions</a>
in
U.S.
and
for
<a
href="/wiki/Kiss_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Kiss
(band)">Kiss</a>
in
Europe.</p>








<p>In
1985,
Bon
Jovi's
second
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/7800%C2%B0_Fahrenheit?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="7800&deg;
Fahrenheit">7800&deg;
Fahrenheit</a></i>
was
released.
The
band
released
three
singles
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Only_Lonely?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Only
Lonely">Only
Lonely</a>&quot;,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/In_and_Out_of_Love_(Bon_Jovi_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="In
and
Out
of
Love
(Bon
Jovi
song)">In
and
Out
of
Love</a>&quot;
and
the
ballad
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Silent_Night_(Bon_Jovi_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Silent
Night
(Bon
Jovi
song)">Silent
Night</a>&quot;.
The
album
peaked
at
number
thirty
seven
on
Billboard
200
and
certified
Gold
by
<a
href="/wiki/RIAA?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="RIAA"
class="mw-redirect">RIAA</a>.
While
the
album
did
not
do
as
well
as
they'd
hoped
in
terms
of
sales,
it
allowed
Bon
Jovi
to
get
out
on
the
road
touring
again.
In
May
1985,
Bon
Jovi
headlined
venues
in
Japan
and
Europe.
At
the
end
of
the
European
tour,
the
band
began
a
six-month
run
of
U.S.
tour
dates
supporting
<a
href="/wiki/Ratt?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Ratt">Ratt</a>.
In
the
midst
of
that
tour
they
managed
to
make
appearances
at
the
Texas
Jam
and
Castle
Donington's
<a
href="/wiki/Monsters_of_Rock?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Monsters
of
Rock">Monsters
of
Rock</a>
concerts
in
England.
Jon
Bon
Jovi
also
did
a
solo
appearance
at
the
very
first
<a
href="/wiki/Farm_Aid?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Farm
Aid">Farm
Aid</a>
in
1985.</p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Slippery_When_Wet_.281986.E2.80.931987.29"><i>Slippery
When
Wet</i>
(1986–1987)</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Bon_Jovi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4"
title="Edit
section:
Slippery
When
Wet
(1986–1987)">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>After
two
moderately
successful
albums,
the
group
changed
their
approach
for
their
next
album
and
hired
professional
songwriter
<a
href="/wiki/Desmond_Child?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Desmond
Child">Desmond
Child</a>
as
a
collaborator.
<a
href="/wiki/Bruce_Fairbairn?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bruce
Fairbairn">Bruce
Fairbairn</a>
was
chosen
as
the
producer
of
the
album.
In
early
1986
Bon
Jovi
moved
to
<a
href="/wiki/Vancouver?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Vancouver">Vancouver</a>,
Canada
to
record
their
third
album.
The
band
spent
six-months
recording
the
new
album.
The
band
decided
to
name
the
album
&quot;Slippery
When
Wet&quot;
after
visiting
a
strip
club
in
Vancouver<sup
id="cite_ref-TV_10-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-TV-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>On
August
16,
1986,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Slippery_When_Wet?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Slippery
When
Wet">Slippery
When
Wet</a></i>
was
released.
The
album
reached
number
one
in
U.S.,
where
it
spent
8
weeks
at
number
one
on
the
<a
href="/wiki/Billboard_200?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Billboard
200"><i>Billboard</i>
200</a>
album
chart.<sup
id="cite_ref-11"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-12"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
first
two
singles
from
the
album,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/You_Give_Love_a_Bad_Name_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="You
Give
Love
a
Bad
Name
(song)">You
Give
Love
a
Bad
Name</a>&quot;
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Livin%27_on_a_Prayer?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Livin'
on
a
Prayer">Livin'
on
a
Prayer</a>&quot;,
both
reached
number
one
on
the
<a
href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Billboard
Hot
100"><i>Billboard</i>
Hot
100</a>
singles
chart.<sup
id="cite_ref-allmusicsingles_13-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-allmusicsingles-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup>
Slippery
When
Wet
was
named
the
top
selling
album
of
1987
by
<i><a
href="/wiki/Billboard_(magazine)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Billboard
(magazine)">Billboard</a></i><sup
id="cite_ref-billboard_14-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-billboard-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup>
&quot;Livin'
On
A
Prayer&quot;
won
an
<a
href="/wiki/MTV_Video_Music_Award?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="MTV
Video
Music
Award">MTV
Video
Music
Award</a>
for
Best
Stage
Performance.<sup
id="cite_ref-metrolyrics.com_15-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-metrolyrics.com-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
band
won
an
award
for
Favorite
Pop/Rock
Band
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/American_Music_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="American
Music
Awards"
class="mw-redirect">American
Music
Awards</a><sup
id="cite_ref-american-music-awards_16-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-american-music-awards-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
an
award
for
Favorite
Rock
Group
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/People%27s_Choice_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="People's
Choice
Awards">People's
Choice
Awards</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-1988_People.27s_Choice_.C3.96d.C3.BClleri_17-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-1988_People.27s_Choice_.C3.96d.C3.BClleri-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup>
When
<i>Slippery
When
Wet</i>
was
released
in
August
1986,
Bon
Jovi
was
the
support
act
for
<a
href="/wiki/38_Special_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="38
Special
(band)">38
Special</a>.
By
the
end
of
1986,
Bon
Jovi
were
well
into
six
months
of
headline
dates
in
arenas
across
America.
In
August
1987,
the
band
headlined
England's
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Monsters_of_Rock?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Monsters
of
Rock">Monsters
of
Rock</a>&quot;
festival.
During
their
set
<a
href="/wiki/Dee_Snider?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Dee
Snider">Dee
Snider</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Bruce_Dickinson?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bruce
Dickinson">Bruce
Dickinson</a>
and
Paul
Stanley
joined
the
band
to
perform
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/We%27re_an_American_Band_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="We're
an
American
Band
(song)">We're
an
American
Band</a>&quot;.
The
band
ended
the
year
having
headlined
130
shows
in
the
&quot;Tour
Without
End&quot;,
grossing
$28,400,000.</p>








<p>Jon
Bon
Jovi
was
asked
what
this
breakthrough
to
worldwide
fame
meant,
to
which
he
answered,
&quot;Everything
is
bigger,
and
it
moves
twice
as
fast.
You're
recognized
twice
as
often.
This
is
bigger,
the
whole
world
gets
bigger.
You
have
to
sell
more
records,
be
huger.
You
get
smarter
and
you
understand
the
business
a
little
more,
so
it's
more
responsibility.
You
understand
it
now,
and
you
want
to
make
sure
everything
goes
right&quot;.</p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="New_Jersey_and_hiatus_.281988.E2.80.931991.29"><i>New
Jersey</i>
and
hiatus
(1988–1991)</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Bon_Jovi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5"
title="Edit
section:
New
Jersey
and
hiatus
(1988–1991)">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>Determined
to
prove
that
the
success
of
<i>Slippery
When
Wet</i>
was
not
a
fluke,
Bon
Jovi
released
their
fourth
effort
<i><a
href="/wiki/New_Jersey_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="New
Jersey
(album)">New
Jersey</a></i>
in
September
1988.
<i>New
Jersey</i>
peaked
at
number
one
in
US,
Canada,
UK,
Ireland,
New
Zealand
and
Australia.
The
album
produced
five
Top
10
hits
on
the
Billboard
Hot
100,
giving
Bon
Jovi
the
record
for
the
most
Top
10
singles
spawned
by
a
hard
rock
album.<sup
id="cite_ref-18"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup>
Two
of
the
hits,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Bad_Medicine_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bad
Medicine
(song)">Bad
Medicine</a>&quot;
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/I%27ll_Be_There_for_You_(Bon_Jovi_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="I'll
Be
There
for
You
(Bon
Jovi
song)">I'll
Be
There
for
You</a>&quot;,
managed
to
reach
number
one.<sup
id="cite_ref-bjbio_19-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-bjbio-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
album's
three
other
singles
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Born_to_Be_My_Baby?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Born
to
Be
My
Baby">Born
to
Be
My
Baby</a>&quot;,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Lay_Your_Hands_on_Me?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Lay
Your
Hands
on
Me">Lay
Your
Hands
on
Me</a>&quot;,
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Living_in_Sin_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Living
in
Sin
(song)">Living
in
Sin</a>&quot;
reached
the
top
ten.
Bon
Jovi
even
made
the
news
when
the
video
for
&quot;Living
In
Sin&quot;
was
banned
by
MTV
for
featuring
some
too
racy
romance/sex
scenes.
After
that
it
was
re-edited
and
MTV
put
it
in
heavy
rotation.</p>

<p>Bon
Jovi
mounted
another
huge
worldwide
tour
that
continued
throughout
1989
and
1990.
They
visited
more
than
22
countries
and
performed
more
than
232
shows
before
it
was
all
over.
The
personal
highpoint
for
the
band
was
their
June
11,
1989
sell-out
homecoming
at
<a
href="/wiki/Giants_Stadium?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Giants
Stadium">Giants
Stadium</a>
in
New
Jersey.
In
August
1989,
the
band
headed
to
the
Soviet
Union
for
the
<a
href="/wiki/Moscow_Music_Peace_Festival?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Moscow
Music
Peace
Festival">Moscow
Music
Peace
Festival</a>.
Bon
Jovi
were
the
first
band
officially
sanctioned
by
the
Soviet
government
to
perform
in
the
Soviet
Union
and
<i><a
href="/wiki/New_Jersey_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="New
Jersey
(album)">New
Jersey</a></i>
became
the
first
U.S.
album
to
be
released
legally
in
the
<a
href="/wiki/U.S.S.R.?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="U.S.S.R."
class="mw-redirect">U.S.S.R.</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-historyking_1-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-historyking-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-U.S.S.R._20-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-U.S.S.R.-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
September
1989,
Jon
Bon
Jovi
and
Richie
Sambora
performed
Livin'
On
A
Prayer
and
Wanted
Dead
Or
Alive
only
with
two
acoustic
guitars
on
the
<a
href="/wiki/1989_MTV_Video_Music_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="1989
MTV
Video
Music
Awards">1989
MTV
Video
Music
Awards</a>.
The
performance
has
generally
been
acknowledged
as
the
inspirational
spark
that
led
to
the
<a
href="/wiki/MTV_Unplugged?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="MTV
Unplugged">MTV
Unplugged</a>
series
and
the
catalyst
for
the
subsequent
popularity
of
the
unplugged
movement
in
popular
music.<sup
id="cite_ref-livinglegends_21-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-livinglegends-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>The
non-stop
touring
was
taking
its
toll
on
the
band.
By
the
end
of
the
New
Jersey
tour,
Bon
Jovi
had
16
months
of
concerts
under
their
belt
and
the
band
members
were
exhausted
physically,
mentally
and
emotionally.
Finally,
following
the
last
tour
date
in
Mexico,
and
without
any
clear
plans
for
their
future,
the
band
members
just
went
home.</p>








<p>Between
1990
and
1991
the
band
members
went
their
separate
ways.
The
exhaustion
of
recording
both
Slippery
When
Wet
and
New
Jersey
back
to
back,
with
highly
paced
world
tours
after
each
album,
took
its
toll
on
the
band.
The
band
has
since
stated
that
there
were
few
if
any
goodbyes
between
them
at
the
end
of
the
New
Jersey
tour.
During
the
time
they
took
off
from
the
scene,
the
band
retreated
to
<a
href="/wiki/Bon_Jovi?qsrc=3044#Solo_projects"
title="Bon
Jovi">their
own
projects</a>
and
showed
no
desire
for
making
another
album.</p>








<p>Disillusioned
with
the
music
business,
despite
all
his
success,
and
unhappy
with
the
status
quo,
in
1991
Jon
Bon
Jovi
fired
his
management,
business
advisers,
and
agents,
including
his
long-time
manager,
Doc
McGhee.
Jon
took
on
the
quarterbacking
responsibilities
himself
by
closing
ranks
and
creating
<i>Bon
Jovi
Management</i>.
In
October
1991
the
band
went
to
a
<a
href="/wiki/Caribbean_island?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Caribbean
island"
class="mw-redirect">Caribbean
island</a>
of
<a
href="/wiki/Saint_Thomas,_U.S._Virgin_Islands?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Saint
Thomas,
U.S.
Virgin
Islands">St.
Thomas</a>
to
discuss
plans
for
the
future.
They
managed
to
resolve
their
differences
by
allowing
each
member
to
speak
about
his
feelings
without
interruption
from
each
other.<sup
class="Template-Fact"
style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a
href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed"
target="_blank"
title="Wikipedia:Citation
needed"><span
title="This
claim
needs
references
to
reliable
sources.
(June
2013)">citation
needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
Upon
resolving
their
issues,
they
headed
back
into
the
Vancouver
Little
Mountain
studios
with
<a
href="/wiki/Bob_Rock?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bob
Rock">Bob
Rock</a>
to
work
on
the
band's
fifth
album
in
January
1992.</p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Keep_the_Faith_and_Cross_Road_.281992-1995.29"><i>Keep
the
Faith</i>
and
<i>Cross
Road</i>
(1992-1995)</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Bon_Jovi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6"
title="Edit
section:
Keep
the
Faith
and
Cross
Road
(1992-1995)">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>Bon
Jovi's
fifth
studio
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/Keep_the_Faith?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Keep
the
Faith">Keep
the
Faith</a></i>
was
released
in
November
1992,
representing
&quot;the
beginning
of
a
new
chapter
in
the
history
of
Bon
Jovi&quot;
and
marking
a
change
in
the
band's
sound
and
image.
The
album
turned
away
from
heavy
drums
and
wild
guitar
solos,
but
instead
introduced
a
more
mature
sound
of
Bon
Jovi
and
contained
more
serious
lyrics.
The
media
focused
considerable
attention
on
Jon
Bon
Jovi’s
hair.
When
Jon
Bon
Jovi
cut
his
hair
he
made
headlines
on
<a
href="/wiki/CNN?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="CNN">CNN</a>.
To
promote
<i>Keep
The
Faith</i>
they
returned
to
their
roots
playing
a
few
dates
at
the
small
New
Jersey
clubs
where
they
had
started
their
career.
The
band
appeared
on
<i><a
href="/wiki/MTV_Unplugged?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="MTV
Unplugged">MTV
Unplugged</a></i>
but
that
was
different
from
the
other
episodes
of
MTV
Unplugged
series.
The
performance
captures
Bon
Jovi
in
an
intimate,
&quot;in
the
round&quot;
experience,
performing
acoustic
and
electric
renditions
of
classic
hits
(Bon
Jovi
and
non-Bon
Jovi
tracks)
and
new
material
from
<i>Keep
the
Faith</i>.
The
concert
was
released
commercially
in
1993
as
<i><a
href="/wiki/Keep_the_Faith:_An_Evening_with_Bon_Jovi?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Keep
the
Faith:
An
Evening
with
Bon
Jovi">Keep
the
Faith:
An
Evening
with
Bon
Jovi</a></i>.</p>








<p>The
album
managed
to
reach
Double
Platinum
status
by
the
RIAA
<sup
id="cite_ref-riaa_22-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-riaa-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
produced
the
Top
10
hit
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Bed_of_Roses_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bed
of
Roses
(song)">Bed
of
Roses</a>&quot;
while
the
<a
href="/wiki/Keep_the_Faith_(Bon_Jovi_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Keep
the
Faith
(Bon
Jovi
song)">title
track</a>
hit
number
one
on
the
<a
href="/wiki/Mainstream_Rock_Tracks?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Mainstream
Rock
Tracks"
class="mw-redirect">Mainstream
Rock
Tracks</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-allmusicsingles_13-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-allmusicsingles-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup>
Bon
Jovi
embarked
on
an
extensive
international
world
tour
for
the
album,
visiting
countries
the
band
had
never
seen
before
and
headlining
stadiums
in
the
South
America,
Europe,
Asia
and
Australia.
They
visited
37
countries,
performed
177
shows
and
seen
them
play
to
2.5
million
fans
on
the
<a
href="/wiki/Keep_the_Faith_Tour?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Keep
the
Faith
Tour">Keep
the
Faith
Tour</a>/<a
href="/wiki/I%27ll_Sleep_When_I%27m_Dead_Tour?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="I'll
Sleep
When
I'm
Dead
Tour">I'll
Sleep
When
I'm
Dead
Tour</a>.</p>








<p>In
October
1994,
Bon
Jovi
released
a
<a
href="/wiki/Greatest_hits?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Greatest
hits"
class="mw-redirect">greatest
hits</a>
album
titled
<i><a
href="/wiki/Cross_Road?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Cross
Road">Cross
Road</a></i>,
with
two
new
tracks:
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Always_(Bon_Jovi_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Always
(Bon
Jovi
song)">Always</a>&quot;
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Someday_I%27ll_Be_Saturday_Night?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Someday
I'll
Be
Saturday
Night">Someday
I'll
Be
Saturday
Night</a>&quot;.
The
first
single
from
the
album
&quot;Always&quot;
became
Bon
Jovi's
highest
selling
single
and
stayed
on
top
ten
of
the
<a
href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Billboard
Hot
100">Billboard
Hot
100</a>
for
six
months.
In
the
UK,
<i>Cross
Road</i>
became
the
best-selling
album
of
1994.
That
year
Bon
Jovi
won
an
award
for
<i>Best
Selling
Rock
Band</i>
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/World_Music_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="World
Music
Awards">World
Music
Awards</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-23"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>That
same
year,
bassist
Alec
John
Such
was
fired
from
the
band,
the
first
lineup
change
since
Bon
Jovi
began.
<a
href="/wiki/Hugh_McDonald_(American_musician)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hugh
McDonald
(American
musician)">Hugh
McDonald</a>
who
was
the
bassist
on
&quot;Runaway,&quot;
unofficially
replaced
Such
as
bassist.
Jon
Bon
Jovi
said,
regarding
the
departure
of
Such:
&quot;Of
course
it
hurts.
But
I
learned
to
accept
and
respect
it.
The
fact
that
I'm
a
workaholic,
studio
in,
studio
out,
stage
on,
stage
off,
want
to
be
dealing
with
music
day
and
night,
doesn't
mean
everyone
else
has
to
adjust
to
that
pace.
Alec
wanted
to
quit
for
a
while
now,
so
it
didn't
come
as
a
complete
surprise.&quot;</p>








<p>It
was
followed
by
hugely
succesfull
world
wide
tour.
In
June
1995,
Bon
Jovi
sold
out
three-nights
at
London's
historical
<i><a
href="/wiki/Wembley_Stadium?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Wembley
Stadium">Wembley
Stadium</a></i>.
The
concerts
were
documented
for
<i>Bon
Jovi:
<a
href="/wiki/Live_From_London_(Bon_Jovi)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Live
From
London
(Bon
Jovi)"
class="mw-redirect">Live
From
London</a></i>.</p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="These_Days_and_another_hiatus_.281995-1998.29"><i>These
Days</i>
and
another
hiatus
(1995-1998)</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Bon_Jovi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7"
title="Edit
section:
These
Days
and
another
hiatus
(1995-1998)">edit</a>]</span></h3>

<p>Bon
Jovi's
sixth
studio
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/These_Days_(Bon_Jovi_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="These
Days
(Bon
Jovi
album)">These
Days</a></i>,
was
released
in
June
1995,
during
which
time
the
band
on
European
tour.
The
album
debuted
at
number
one
in
UK
and
spent
four
consecutive
weeks
at
the
top
position.
The
album
also
reached
number
one
in
Ireland,
Germany,
Australia,
Japan
and
many
other
countries.
The
album's
first
single
was
the
<a
href="/wiki/Rhythm_and_blues?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rhythm
and
blues">rhythm
and
blues</a>
influenced
ballad
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/This_Ain%27t_a_Love_Song?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="This
Ain't
a
Love
Song">This
Ain't
a
Love
Song</a>&quot;.
With
an
exotic
video
filmed
in
Thailand,
&quot;This
Ain't
a
Love
Song&quot;
reached
top
twenty
on
the
Billboard
Hot
100,
and
was
the
only
significant
US
hit
from
the
album,
however,
the
album
produced
four
UK
top
ten
hits
(&quot;This
Aint
A
Love
Song&quot;,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Something_for_the_Pain?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Something
for
the
Pain">Something
for
the
Pain</a>&quot;,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Lie_to_Me?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Lie
to
Me">Lie
to
Me</a>&quot;
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/These_Days_(Bon_Jovi_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="These
Days
(Bon
Jovi
song)">These
Days</a>&quot;).
That
year
the
band
earned
a
<a
href="/wiki/BRIT_Award?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="BRIT
Award"
class="mw-redirect">BRIT
Award</a>
for
best
international
band
and
also
won
a
<a
href="/wiki/MTV_Europe_Music_Award?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="MTV
Europe
Music
Award"
class="mw-redirect">MTV
Europe
Music
Award</a>
for
Best
Rock.
It
was
followed
by
These
Days
Tour.
In
June
1995,
Bon
Jovi
sold
out
three-nights
at
London's
historical
<i><a
href="/wiki/Wembley_Stadium?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Wembley
Stadium">Wembley
Stadium</a></i>.
The
concerts
were
documented
for
<i>Bon
Jovi:
<a
href="/wiki/Live_From_London_(Bon_Jovi)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Live
From
London
(Bon
Jovi)"
class="mw-redirect">Live
From
London</a></i>.
Bon
Jovi
visited
43
countries
and
performed
126
shows
on
<i><a
href="/wiki/These_Days_Tour?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="These
Days
Tour">These
Days
Tour</a></i>.</p>








<p>Following
the
overwhelming
success
of
the
<i>These
Days
Tour</i>,
the
members
of
Bon
Jovi
went
their
separate
ways.
But
unlike
the
period
following
the
New
Jersey
tour,
tainted
with
uncertainty,
this
hiatus
was
a
conscious
group
decision.
The
members
of
Bon
Jovi
agreed
to
a
self-imposed
two-year
sabbatical
from
the
band.</p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Crush_and_Bounce_.281999.E2.80.932004.29"><i>Crush</i>
and
<i>Bounce</i>
(1999–2004)</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Bon_Jovi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8"
title="Edit
section:
Crush
and
Bounce
(1999–2004)">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>Bon
Jovi
reunited
in
1999
to
record
the
song
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Real_Life_(Bon_Jovi_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Real
Life
(Bon
Jovi
song)">Real
Life</a>&quot;
for
the
movie
<i><a
href="/wiki/EdTV?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="EdTV"
class="mw-redirect">EdTV</a></i>.
David
Bryan
was
recovering
from
an
accident
in
which
he
nearly
severed
his
finger.</p>








<p>After
a
nearly
four-year
hiatus,
during
which
several
band
members
worked
on
independent
projects,
Bon
Jovi
regrouped
in
1999
to
begin
work
on
their
next
studio
album.
In
June
2000,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Crush_(Bon_Jovi_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Crush
(Bon
Jovi
album)">Crush</a></i>
was
released
as
the
band's
seventh
studio
album
and
constituted
something
of
a
comeback.
The
first
single
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/It%27s_My_Life_(Bon_Jovi_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="It's
My
Life
(Bon
Jovi
song)">It's
My
Life</a>&quot;
was
noted
as
one
of
the
group’s
most
successful
releases
in
a
decade
and
most
importantly,
becoming
a
symbol
of
the
band's
longevity
as
they
prevailed
through
many
different
changes
in
the
mainstream
rock
scene
with
admirable
success.
It's
My
Life
helped
introduce
them
to
a
new,
younger
fan
base.
The
band
received
two
<a
href="/wiki/Grammy?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Grammy"
class="mw-redirect">Grammy</a>
nominations
for
Best
Rock
Album
<i>Crush</i>
and
Best
Rock
Performance
by
Duo/Group
&quot;It's
My
Life&quot;.
The
video
for
&quot;It's
My
Life&quot;
won
the
<a
href="/wiki/My_VH1_Music_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="My
VH1
Music
Awards">My
VH1
Music
Awards</a>
for
&quot;My
Favorite
Video&quot;.</p>








<p>Bon
Jovi
played
two
sold-out
concerts
at
London's
historic
<a
href="/wiki/Wembley_Stadium_(1923)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Wembley
Stadium
(1923)">Wembley
Stadium</a>
in
August
19,
20,
2000,
becoming
the
last
ever
concerts
held
at
the
legendary
venue
before
its
demolition.
That
year
the
band
played
to
1.1
million
fans
in
40
arena
and
stadium
venues
across
North
America,
Europe
and
Japan.
While
on
tour,
Bon
Jovi
released
a
collection
of
live
performances
from
throughout
their
career
in
an
album
entitled
<i><a
href="/wiki/One_Wild_Night_Live_1985%E2%80%932001?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="One
Wild
Night
Live
1985–2001">One
Wild
Night
Live
1985–2001</a></i>.
This
was
Bon
Jovi's
first-ever
live
album.
The
songs
were
culled
from
archives
of
recorded
material
the
band
had
been
collecting
from
their
earliest
days
on
the
road
right
through
the
current
tour.
The
band
sold
out
two
homecoming
concerts
at
New
Jersey's
<a
href="/wiki/Giants_Stadium?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Giants
Stadium">Giants
Stadium</a>
in
July
27,
28,
2001.
The
broadcast
broke
ratings
records
for
the
VH-1
network.
At
the
end
of
the
year
Bon
Jovi
awarded
for
&quot;Hottest
Live
Show&quot;
at
the
2001
<a
href="/wiki/My_VH1_Music_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="My
VH1
Music
Awards">My
VH1
Music
Awards</a>.</p>








<p>The
members
of
the
band
had
anticipated
a
brief
vacation
before
work
would
begin
on
the
band's
8th
studio
album.
But
on
September
11,
the
world
changed.
Within
days
of
the
terrorist
attacks,
Jon
Bon
Jovi
and
Richie
Sambora
had
filmed
Public
Service
Announcements
for
the
Red
Cross,
recorded
&quot;America
The
Beautiful&quot;
for
the
<a
href="/wiki/NFL?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="NFL"
class="mw-redirect">NFL</a>
and
performed
as
part
of
the
historic
<i><a
href="/wiki/America:_A_Tribute_to_Heroes?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="America:
A
Tribute
to
Heroes">America:
A
Tribute
to
Heroes</a></i>
live
telethon.
One
month
later,
the
band
participated
at
two
Monmouth
County
Alliance
of
Neighbors
concerts
in
Red
Bank,
NJ
to
raise
funds
for
the
families
close
the
band's
hometowns,
which
were
affected
by
the
World
Trade
Center
disaster.
And
on
October
21,
2001,
Bon
Jovi
performed
at
the
monumental
<i>Concert
For
New
York</i>
at
<a
href="/wiki/Madison_Square_Garden?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Madison
Square
Garden">Madison
Square
Garden</a>,
raising
relief
funds
and
honoring
those
who
worked
to
save
lives
during
the
attack.
.</p>








<p>In
spring
2002,
the
group
entered
the
studio
to
begin
recording
their
eighth
studio
album.
<i><a
href="/wiki/Bounce_(Bon_Jovi_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bounce
(Bon
Jovi
album)">Bounce</a></i>
was
influenced
by
the
<a
href="/wiki/September_11,_2001_attacks?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="September
11,
2001
attacks"
class="mw-redirect">September
11,
2001
terrorist
attacks</a>,
released
on
October
8,
2002.
The
album
debuted
at
number
two
in
both
the
US
and
UK
.
The
band
went
on
the
<a
href="/wiki/Bounce_Tour?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bounce
Tour">Bounce
Tour</a>
for
the
album,
during
which
they
made
history
as
the
last
band
to
play
<a
href="/wiki/Veterans_Stadium?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Veterans
Stadium">Veterans
Stadium</a>
in
<a
href="/wiki/Philadelphia?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Philadelphia">Philadelphia</a>
before
it
was
torn
down.</p>








<p>Following
the
end
of
the
Bounce
Tour
in
August
2003,
Bon
Jovi
embarked
on
a
side
project;
originally
intending
to
produce
an
album
consisting
of
live
acoustic
performances,
the
band
ended
up
rewriting,
re-recording
and
reinventing
12
of
their
biggest
hits
in
a
new
and
much
different
light.
<i><a
href="/wiki/This_Left_Feels_Right?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="This
Left
Feels
Right">This
Left
Feels
Right</a></i>
was
released
in
November
2003.</p>








<p>The
following
year,
the
band
released
a
box
set
entitled
<i><a
href="/wiki/100,000,000_Bon_Jovi_Fans_Can%27t_Be_Wrong?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="100,000,000
Bon
Jovi
Fans
Can't
Be
Wrong">100,000,000
Bon
Jovi
Fans
Can't
Be
Wrong</a></i>,
the
title
being
a
homage
to
Elvis
Presley's
<i><a
href="/wiki/50,000,000_Elvis_Fans_Can%27t_Be_Wrong?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="50,000,000
Elvis
Fans
Can't
Be
Wrong">50,000,000
Elvis
Fans
Can't
Be
Wrong</a></i>.
The
set
consisted
of
four
CDs
packed
with
38
unreleased
and
12
rare
tracks,
as
well
as
a
DVD.
The
box
set
marked
the
sales
of
100
million
Bon
Jovi
albums
and
also
commemorated
the
20th
anniversary
of
the
release
of
the
band's
first
record
in
1984.
In
November
2004,
Bon
Jovi
was
honored
with
the
Award
for
Merit
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/American_Music_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="American
Music
Awards"
class="mw-redirect">American
Music
Awards</a>.</p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Have_a_Nice_Day_and_Lost_Highway_.282005.E2.80.932008.29"><i>Have
a
Nice
Day</i>
and
<i>Lost
Highway</i>
(2005–2008)</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Bon_Jovi&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9"
title="Edit
section:
Have
a
Nice
Day
and
Lost
Highway
(2005–2008)">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>The
band's
ninth
studio
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Have_a_Nice_Day_(Bon_Jovi_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Have
a
Nice
Day
(Bon
Jovi
album)">Have
a
Nice
Day</a></i>,
was
released
in
September
2005.
The
album
debuted
at
number
two
in
both
the
US
and
UK,
reaching
number
one
in
fifteen
countries.<sup
id="cite_ref-24"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
title
track
was
an
international
hit,
reaching
the
top
ten
in
the
UK,
Europe,
Australia
and
Canada.
The
second
single,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Who_Says_You_Can%27t_Go_Home?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Who
Says
You
Can't
Go
Home">Who
Says
You
Can't
Go
Home</a>&quot;,
was
released
in
early
2006.
The
song
reached
top
forty
on
the
Billboard
Hot
100
in
US.
A
duet
version
of
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Who_Says_You_Can%27t_Go_Home?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Who
Says
You
Can't
Go
Home">Who
Says
You
Can't
Go
Home</a>&quot;
with
country
singer
<a
href="/wiki/Jennifer_Nettles?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Jennifer
Nettles">Jennifer
Nettles</a>
of
the
band
<a
href="/wiki/Sugarland_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Sugarland
(band)"
class="mw-redirect">Sugarland</a>,
peaked
at
number
one
on
the
Billboard
<a
href="/wiki/Hot_Country_Songs?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hot
Country
Songs">Hot
Country
Songs</a>
and
Bon
Jovi
became
the
first
rock
band
to
have
a
number
one
single
on
Billboard's
Country
Chart.
On
February
11,
2007,
Bon
Jovi
and
Jennifer
Nettles
won
the
<a
href="/wiki/Grammy_Award?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Grammy
Award">Grammy
Award</a>,
for
&quot;Best
Country
Collaboration
with
Vocals&quot;
for
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Who_Says_You_Can%27t_Go_Home?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Who
Says
You
Can't
Go
Home">Who
Says
You
Can't
Go
Home</a>&quot;.
The
band
also
won
an
award
for
Favorite
Rock
Song
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/People%27s_Choice_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="People's
Choice
Awards">People's
Choice
Awards</a>
with
&quot;Who
Says
You
Can't
Go
Home&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-2007_People.27s_Choice_.C3.96d.C3.BClleri_25-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-2007_People.27s_Choice_.C3.96d.C3.BClleri-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Soon
after
the
release
of
<i>Have
A
Nice
Day</i>,
the
band
started
gearing
up
for
the
new
2005–2006
worldwide
<a
href="/wiki/Have_A_Nice_Day_Tour?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Have
A
Nice
Day
Tour"
class="mw-redirect">Have
A
Nice
Day
Tour</a>.
This
tour,
took
the
band
to
numerous
stages
and
stadiums
throughout
the
world.
The
tour
was
a
significant
commercial
success,
as
the
group
played
to
2,002,000
fans,
and
the
tour
grossed
a
total
$191
million.
The
tour
was
the
third-highest-grossing
tour
of
2006
taking
in
just
over
$131
million,
just
behind
<a
href="/wiki/The_Rolling_Stones?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Rolling
Stones">The
Rolling
Stones</a>'
<a
href="/wiki/A_Bigger_Bang_World_Tour?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="A
Bigger
Bang
World
Tour"
class="mw-redirect">A
Bigger
Bang
World
Tour</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Madonna_(entertainer)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Madonna
(entertainer)">Madonna</a>'s
<a
href="/wiki/Confessions_Tour?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Confessions
Tour">Confessions
Tour</a>.
On
November
14,
2006,
Bon
Jovi
were
inducted
into
the
<a
href="/wiki/UK_Music_Hall_of_Fame?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="UK
Music
Hall
of
Fame">UK
Music
Hall
of
Fame</a>
alongside
<a
href="/wiki/James_Brown?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="James
Brown">James
Brown</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Led_Zeppelin?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Led
Zeppelin">Led
Zeppelin</a>.</p>








<p>In
June
2007,
Bon
Jovi
released
their
tenth
studio
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Lost_Highway_(Bon_Jovi_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Lost
Highway
(Bon
Jovi
album)">Lost
Highway</a></i>.
The
album
influences
the
band's
rock
sound
with
that
of
country
music
following
the
success
of
a
country
version
of
the
band's
2006
single
&quot;Who
Says
You
Can't
Go
Home&quot;,
a
duet
with
Jennifer
Nettles.
To
promote
the
new
album,
Bon
Jovi
made
several
television
appearances,
including
the
6th
annual
<a
href="/wiki/Country_Music_Television?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Country
Music
Television">CMT</a>
Awards
in
Nashville,
<i><a
href="/wiki/American_Idol?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="American
Idol">American
Idol</a></i>,
and
MTV
Unplugged,
as
well
as
playing
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/Live_Earth_concert,_New_York_City?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Live
Earth
concert,
New
York
City">Live
Earth
concert
at
Giants
Stadium</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-26"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup>
They
also
performed
ten
promotional
gigs
in
the
U.S.,
Canada,
the
UK
and
Japan.
As
part
of
the
'tour',
Bon
Jovi
were
the
first
group
to
perform
at
London's
new
<a
href="/wiki/The_O2_Arena_(London)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
O2
Arena
(London)"
class="mw-redirect">O<sub>2</sub>
Arena</a>
(formerly
the
Millennium
Dome)
when
it
opened
to
the
public
on
June
24,
2007.
The
23,000-seater
stadium
sold
out
within
30
minutes
of
tickets
being
released.<sup
id="cite_ref-BBC_O2_story_27-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-BBC_O2_story-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>The
album,
described
by
Jon
Bon
Jovi
as
a
&quot;Bon
Jovi
album
influenced
by
Nashville&quot;,
topped
the
charts
in
US,
Canada,
Europe,
and
Japan.
The
album's
third
single
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Till_We_Ain%27t_Strangers_Anymore?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Till
We
Ain't
Strangers
Anymore">Till
We
Ain't
Strangers
Anymore</a>&quot;
features
<a
href="/wiki/LeAnn_Rimes?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="LeAnn
Rimes">LeAnn
Rimes</a>,
won
the
<a
href="/wiki/CMT_Music_Award?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="CMT
Music
Award"
class="mw-redirect">CMT
Music
Award</a>
for
the
Collaborative
Video
of
the
Year
in
2008.<sup
id="cite_ref-28"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-cmt_29-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-cmt-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
song
was
also
nominated
for
the
<a
href="/wiki/Academy_of_Country_Music_Award?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Academy
of
Country
Music
Award"
class="mw-redirect">Academy
of
Country
Music
Award</a>
for
Vocal
Event
of
the
Year.<sup
id="cite_ref-30"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
October
2007
the
band
announced
the
<a
href="/wiki/Lost_Highway_Tour?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Lost
Highway
Tour">Lost
Highway
Tour</a>.
Starting
with
the
10
shows
to
open
the
brand
new,
<a
href="/wiki/Newark,_New_Jersey?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Newark,
New
Jersey">Newark,
New
Jersey</a>
<a
href="/wiki/Prudential_Center?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Prudential
Center">Prudential
Center</a>,
the
band
toured
Canada,
Japan,
Australia,
New
Zealand,
the
U.S.
and
then
Europe,
finishing
in
the
summer
of
2008.
The
tour
was
the
highest
grossing
tour
of
2008
in
Billboard's
rankings,
with
ticket
sales
of
$210.6
million,
reported
from
November
14,
2007
through
Nov.11,
2008.<sup
id="cite_ref-bb121108_31-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-bb121108-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
all,
2,157,675
tickets
were
sold
during
2008.<sup
id="cite_ref-bb121108_31-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-bb121108-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup>
Combined
with
$16.4
million
in
2007
from
the
Newark
shows,
making
a
combined
gross
of
$227
million
in
ticket
sales.
In
<a
href="/wiki/Pollstar?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Pollstar">Pollstar</a>'s
calculus
for
North
America,
the
Lost
Highway
Tour
had
the
highest
gross
for
2008
at
$70.4
million.<sup
id="cite_ref-32"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h3><span

<span

Richie
Sambora
and

at

Tribeca

Festival
